    <li> The product came exactly as I expected it to; a large ivory block sealed in a plastic bag. Upon taking it out, the bag was very messy and my fingers were covered in thick butter. I tried to pack it into a plastic container to use as a body butter later, but I could tell that this was not a one-step process. I looked through a bunch of YouTube videos, and here&#x27;s what I came up with (so you don&#x27;t have to):&lt;br /&gt;Soft Whipped Body Butter:&lt;br /&gt;1. Cut the block into chunks and either stick it in the microwave for a few minutes, or seal the container and soak in hot water until it is melted. Do not let any water get in.&lt;br /&gt;2. Pour the raw melted butter into a large mixing bowl. Having a few chunks is normal, but they should be soft.&lt;br /&gt;3. Add any mixture of the following ingredients: Extra Virgin Olive Oil, Coconut Oil, Carrot Oil, or any other natural ingredient. That&#x27;s just what was in my cabinet at the time. I didn&#x27;t measure, just add what seems about right. (warning: I added a spoonful of Victoria&#x27;s Secret body butter, and it grossly broke up and settled at the bottom. Do not use.)&lt;br /&gt;4. Use a mixer to whip the butter until all of the ingredients are mixed and there are no chunks.&lt;br /&gt;5. Pour into desired container. Leave the cap off, and let it solidify.&lt;br /&gt;6. Now you should have a soft body butter that melts on your skin. Don&#x27;t be alarmed if it feels grainy at first contact- this goes away immediately! Not sure why, but I don&#x27;t mind it. The texture is light and oil-like, and my skin soaks it up like no tomorrow(unlike heavy oils that sit on the skin).&lt;br /&gt;Be warned- it smells gross. But within an hour you can&#x27;t smell a thing. Add your favorite body mist, and you&#x27;ll look and feel baby-smooth for days. I know I do. Best moisturizer I&#x27;ve ever used, don&#x27;t hesitate!  Four stars for being led to believe it was useable as-is.</li>

The highest quality shea butter (used for acne, eczema, arthritis and other medicinal purposes) should be ivory and the consistency of mildly soft butter.  This shea butter, unlike the photo, is a yellow color (which I learned is dyed using plant dyes) and is a harder consistency and has an off odor.  It still works as a moisturizer, but not for the medicinal benefits I was anticipating.     <li> I thought I would make a video review, and maybe I&#x27;ll get to that later, but for now I&#x27;ll just review and tell you how to make your own Shea Butter.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Like everyone else said, it comes double bagged so the packaging isn&#x27;t the best. However, mine was sealed well and not damaged and I was perfectly fine with it. It was true ivory Shea, which generally means pure. It wasn&#x27;t rancid or anything like that either. That smell is what it should smell like if not refined and without additives.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Overall, the quality was very high and quite a bargain when you consider that most products that say they are Shea based contain only a spoon full or two per container in reality. This allows a much higher level of purity for anything you&#x27;d like to Shea up. Very pleased with it and I do plan to re-order. I&#x27;ll be making home made shea butter in custom scents for everyone for Christmas this year!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;That said, it can be a bit difficult to use and does leave a smell when you don&#x27;t doctor it up. So I do. Here is the easiest way to do it for you too.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;To Make Shea Butter:&lt;br /&gt;1) Very slowly melt your shea in a double boiler OR by floating a bowl containing the shea in a large pot. Use very low heat since it melts at body temperature. The more heat, the more vitamins you take out of it so less is better.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;2) Once mostly melted (you can leave some chunks), you can let it settle some to be sure there are no sediments (also normal for unrefined though mine had none) and then pour the liquid carefully into another bowl for mixing, leaving the sediments behind.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;3) Add about 5 ounces of various oils to one pound of Shea. I added 2 ounces of Sweet Almond Oil, 2 ounces of Hazelnut Oil and 1/2 ounce of Wheat Germ Oil and Macadamia Nut Oil each.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;4) Mix using a hand mixer (not your kitchen aid) on whip for a long time. To shorten the time, just mix it enough to fully incorporate the oils (maybe 2 minutes) and then put the bowl into the fridge for 10 minutes. It will form a white layer on top of cooled shea. Then you take it out and keep mixing. It will take so long that you&#x27;ll think you&#x27;re doing it wrong, but you&#x27;re not. Just keep going. Eventually, you&#x27;ll start forming something that looks like frosting that smells a lot better than plain Shea.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;5) Add your scent oils. I use pure essential oils and I made 2 batches. One Rosemary Mint and one Lavendar Orange. Both lovely. You&#x27;ll need to decide your own amounts on this but you don&#x27;t need a whole lot of it. Then mix it in and voila, you&#x27;re done. Spoon into whatever containers you&#x27;d like to use. I used pyrex bowls with the plastic lids.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;6) Makes about 5 pints. It will re-stiffen, but not as much as before, and will spread and melt more easily. Also soaks in a tad faster.he fridge for 10 minutes. It will form a white layer on top of cooled shea. Then you take it out and keep mixing. It will take so long that you&#x27;ll think you&#x27;re doing it wrong, but you&#x27;re not. Just keep going. Eventually, you&#x27;ll start forming something that looks like frosting that smells a lot better than plain Shea.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;5) Add your scent oils. I use pure essential oils and I made 2 batches. One Rosemary Mint and one Lavendar Orange. Both lovely. You&#x27;ll need to decide your own amounts on this but you don&#x27;t need a whole lot of it. Then mix it in and voila, you&#x27;re done. Spoon into whatever containers you&#x27;d like to use. I used pyrex bowls with the plastic lids.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;6) Makes about 5 pints. It will re-stiffen, but not as much as before, and will spread and melt more easily. Also soaks in a tad faster.</li>

    <li> Unrefined shea butter is usually yellow.... it is when it is refined n much like cocoa butter has been bleached or chemically treated to REMOVE the color that it then becomes white. Several natural oils and butters have yellow color because many are derived from nuts etc... which are NOT white... that is the more natural form. Cocoa butter, comes from the cocoa bean, when cocoa liquer is extracted you can then process the fats for said butters. Because some don&#x27;t want a mild chocolate smell it is further refined n bleached etc to remove color.&lt;br /&gt;Shea butter comes from the shea nut.... the remaining butter is yellow.&lt;br /&gt;Milk is white but when churned and curds separated the fats or butter is light yellow...&lt;br /&gt;Goes to reason more natural product that has been less refined would remain more pigmented...&lt;br /&gt;Shea has a distinct smell, but if stored properly and truly organic doesn&#x27;t really \\&quot;go bad\\&quot;. Should not smell rancid, but for a pleasant smelling shea experience usually there are other essential oil scents mixed In.&lt;br /&gt;Shame on a seller that taints the name of such a usually wonderful product.</li>

I also waited to write this review until I was able to order a USDA certified organic, raw, unrefined shea butter from Mountainroseherbs.com to compare it with this product in order to be fair.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I received this product in a thin plastic container with a lid (looked like potato salad that you would order from your local deli), not in a plastic bag as others mentioned.  The faded label on the container said, \\&quot;sold as set...ready to ship\\&quot; with a bar code on it.  There is no organic certification printed anywhere on this product or ingredients - it definitely not USDA organic.  I used quite a bit of the pound that i purchased.  Yes, it did have a strong smell like shea butter, but this one was more pungent and bitter as if it was on the cusp of going bad (Pure, unrefined organic shea butter is a yellow/beige color and their is a a nutty somewhat earthy odor that I am used to.  Some like it and some don&#x27;t.  I don&#x27;t love the smell, but I wouldn&#x27;t use shea butter in any other way, most of the healing properties are destroyed during the refining and bleaching process as is the smell, which is why cosmetics and skin care manufacturers buy it refined - because it eliminates the odor and will last longer.....adding organic essential oils to organic unrefined shea butter can make it smell wonderful - but if your shea butter is white and smells fresh and clean, than it has been been refined and bleached).  I noticed immediately that this shea butter had lumps that seemed more greasy than the non-lump areas if that makes any sense - it had a distinct heavy emollient feel to it. I must admit that it did feel good on my skin, I have dry, sensitive and problematic skin, so I like a thick and hardy cream. I still had an open mind, in fact I referred it to my Mom who bought it as well, plus i read all of the great reviews and the fact that it comes all the way from Ghana......hmmmmm, .&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;Well, I used it to make several lotion, cream, lip balm and healing butter recipes that require melting down shea butter along with beeswax and other carrier oils in a double boiler.  It took longer to melt down the shea butter than it did the beeswax...more than 20 minutes....that was not a good sign.  So, I stopped using it and ordered a pound of shea butter from mountain rose herbs as mentioned above to see how the two products compared.  The quality, consistency and appearance were truly a night and day difference.  The new shea butter was smoother, almost flaky - although thick, it was not chunky.  Additionally, it did not have a heavy feel to it - once you applied it to your skin it melted right in with a slightly thinner consistency. The smell was definitely reminiscent of shea butter, as it should be and when I used it to make the products above, it melted quickly!&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I did see the review where someone mentioned there was petroleum jelly mixed in this product.  I have not tested this product nor will i volunteer to so given the expense, but it felt to me like it was possible something else was mixed in.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I would love to hear what the seller has to say about this shea butter as I have not yet seen a singe response to any of the reviews.  I would also urge the seller to be careful when labeling this product as \\&quot;organic\\&quot; and selling it that way when it is clearly not certified.&lt;br /&gt;&lt;br /&gt;I will not buy this product again.  If you are looking for a natural organic pure and urefined shea butter, this product is not what it claims to be - buyer beware!</li>
